	<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Star (keelboat)</h1>
	
	<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
		<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
		<div id="contentSub"></div>

class</a></th></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The <b>Star</b> is a 6.9 metres (23&#160;ft) one-design racing <a href="/wiki/Keelboat" title="Keelboat">keelboat</a> for two people designed by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Francis_Sweisguth&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Francis Sweisguth (page does not exist)">Francis Sweisguth</a> in 1910. The Star was an <a href="/wiki/Olympic_sailing_classes" title="Olympic sailing classes">Olympic keelboat class</a> from 1932 through to 2012, the last year keelboats appeared at the Summer Olympics.
</p><p>It is <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">sloop</a>-rigged, with a <a href="/wiki/Mainsail" title="Mainsail">mainsail</a> larger in proportional size than any other boat of its length. Unlike most modern racing boats, it does not use a <a href="/wiki/Spinnaker" title="Spinnaker">spinnaker</a> when sailing downwind.  Instead, when running downwind a <a href="/wiki/Whisker_pole" class="mw-redirect" title="Whisker pole">whisker pole</a> is used to hold the <a href="/wiki/Jib" title="Jib">jib</a> out to windward for correct wind flow. Early Stars were built from wood, but modern boats are generally made of <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a>. The boat must weigh at least 671&#160;kg (1,479&#160;lb) with a maximum total sail area of 26.5&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (285&#160;sq&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-Rules-Page_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rules-Page-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Specifications_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Specifications-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Class-Rules_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Class-Rules-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>
The Star class pioneered an unusual circular <a href="/wiki/Boom_vang" title="Boom vang">boom vang</a> track, which allows the vang to effectively hold the boom down even when the boom is turned far outboard on a downwind run. Another notable aspect of Star sailing is the extreme <a href="/wiki/Hiking_(sailing)" title="Hiking (sailing)">hiking</a> position adopted by the crew and at times the helmsman, who normally use a harness to help hang low off the windward side of the boat with only their lower legs inside.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_original.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Star_original.svg/220px-Star_original.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Star_original.svg/330px-Star_original.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Star_original.svg/440px-Star_original.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="428" data-file-height="469" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_original.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Original sail plan (pre-1922)</div></div></div>
<p>The Star was designed in 1910 by Francis Sweisguth, a draftsman at the William Gardner Marine Architect office. Over the course of his career Sweisguth designed a variety of yachts. A more traditional example of his work is Silent Maid, a Barnegat Bay B-class catboat designed shortly after the Star. The first 22 stars were built in <a href="/wiki/Port_Washington,_New_York" title="Port Washington, New York">Port Washington, New York</a> by <a href="/wiki/Isaac_E._Smith" title="Isaac E. Smith">Ike Smith</a> during the winter of 1910–11. Since that time, over 8,400 boats have been built, with more than 2,000 actively racing in 170 fleets.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The hull is a hard <a href="/wiki/Chine_(boating)" title="Chine (boating)">chine</a> design with a slight curve to the bottom section, and a <a href="/wiki/Bulb_keel" title="Bulb keel">bulb keel</a>. The Star was originally rigged with a large, low-aspect-ratio <a href="/wiki/Gunter" title="Gunter">gunter</a> mainsail and jib, which was replaced by a short <a href="/wiki/Bermuda_rig" title="Bermuda rig">bermuda rig</a> in 1921, before the current tall bermuda sail plan was adopted in 1930. In 1965, <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a> replaced wood as the primary hull material. Other changes to the strict design rules for the Star class, include adding flexible <a href="/wiki/Spar_(sailing)" title="Spar (sailing)">spars</a>, an innovative circular-track <a href="/wiki/Boom_vang" title="Boom vang">boom vang</a>, and self-bailers.<sup id="cite_ref-Bird_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events">Events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="86" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4276" data-file-height="1672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_Boats_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Star Boats North American Championships June 2013</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/220px-Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/330px-Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg/440px-Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1828" data-file-height="1436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Star_Boats_3_NHYC_June_2013_photo_D_Ramey_Logan.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Star Boats NHYC North American Championships June 2013</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Olympics">Olympics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Olympics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Star was added to the Olympic roster for the 1932 Summer Olympics in Los Angeles. Due to <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, there were no Olympic games held in 1940 or 1944, and for <a href="/wiki/Sailing_at_the_1976_Summer_Olympics" title="Sailing at the 1976 Summer Olympics">1976</a>, the Star was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Tempest_(keelboat)" title="Tempest (keelboat)">Tempest</a> for keelboat competition. In 2011 keelboats were removed from <a href="/wiki/Sailing_at_the_2016_Summer_Olympics" title="Sailing at the 2016 Summer Olympics">sailing at the 2016 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>. The last keelboat Olympics competition was at the <a href="/wiki/Sailing_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics" title="Sailing at the 2012 Summer Olympics">2012 London Summer Olympics</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Championships">World Championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: World Championships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Star_World_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Star World Championships">Star World Championships</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Star_World_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="Star World Championships">Star World Championships</a> has been held annually since 1923. Most titles has American sailor <a href="/wiki/Lowell_North" title="Lowell North">Lowell North</a> won, with five titles between 1945 and 1973 and another seven podiums. The most crowned skipper-crew combination is Italian duo <a href="/wiki/Agostino_Straulino" title="Agostino Straulino">Agostino Straulino</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nicol%C3%B2_Rode" title="Nicolò Rode">Nicolò Rode</a> and Brazilian duo <a href="/wiki/Torben_Grael" title="Torben Grael">Torben Grael</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_Ferreira" title="Marcelo Ferreira">Marcelo Ferreira</a> with three titles each. Also, American <a href="/wiki/Mark_Reynolds_(sailor)" title="Mark Reynolds (sailor)">Mark Reynolds</a> has three titles, but with different crew.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Star_Sailors_League">Star Sailors League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Star Sailors League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Star_Sailors_League" title="Star Sailors League">Star Sailors League</a> was created in 2013 by athletes to establish a sustainable sailing circuit.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Famous_Star_sailors">Famous Star sailors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Star_(keelboat)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Famous Star sailors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Duarte_Bello" class="mw-redirect" title="Duarte Bello">Duarte Bello</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Championship competitor, 1947–1970s. Invented auto-bailers and circular boom-vang track)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy" title="John F. Kennedy">John F. Kennedy</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Nantucket Sound Star Class Championship: 1936)</span><sup id="cite_ref-Bird_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bird-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Agostino_Straulino" title="Agostino Straulino">Agostino Straulino</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Olympic Champion: 1952; World Champion: 1952, 1953, 1956; Olympic Silver: 1956)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Halperin" title="Robert Halperin">Robert Halperin</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Olympic Bronze: 1960; Pan American Games Gold: 1963)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Paul_Elvstr%C3%B8m" title="Paul Elvstrøm">Paul Elvstrøm</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(World Champion: 1966, 1967)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dennis_Conner" title="Dennis Conner">Dennis Conner</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(World Champion: 1971, 1977)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Buddy_Melges" title="Buddy Melges">Buddy Melges</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(World Champion: 1978, 1979)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Iain_Percy" title="Iain Percy">Iain Percy</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Olympic Champion: 2008; World Champion: 2010; Olympic Silver: 2012)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Scheidt" title="Robert Scheidt">Robert Scheidt</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(Olympic Silver: 2008; Olympic Bronze: 2012; World Champion: 2008, 2011, 2012; SSL Finals: 2013)</span></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fredrik_L%C3%B6%C3%B6f" title="Fredrik Lööf">Fredrik Lööf</a> <span style="font-size:90%">(World Champion: 2001, 2004; Olympic Champion: 2012)</span></li></ul>
